  - Asana automation limitations (Starter plan blocking premium automation features → “keep manual”)

- You outline the hiring process: stack candidates → short interviews → offer → automate training.
- You want outreach to people who submitted initial form but **didn’t** submit Loom (emails go to spam).
- You emphasize speed + consistency (don’t personalize names, filter out people who already did Loom, etc.)

- You explicitly push back on emailing clients; want everything centralized in Discord (no custom workflow per client).

## assistant (2026-02-21T17:03:05.821Z)

If you’re asking “today, with what we’ve seen in Feb 17–Feb 21?”, my take is:

### You shouldn’t keep him in the role *as-is*
The pattern isn’t “one-off mistakes.” It’s repeated execution errors on things that break delivery (GHL setup, tracking accuracy, client comms, links/process). That’s an ops role failing at the core job: reliable, correct execution.

### Fire vs last chance comes down to 2 questions
1) **Is the cost of one more failure unacceptable?**  
   If another Prestige-style miss could cost you clients/cashflow/reputation → lean **fire fast**.

2) **Do you believe he can change within 7–14 days with tight controls?**  
   If yes → give a **short, brutal PIP**. If no → firing is the clean move.

### If you keep him: do a 7-day “proof or done” PIP (not vibes)
Non-negotiables:
- **Daily “Definition of Done” checklist** per client/account (GHL, phone, users, automations, cleanup, etc.)
- **Zero-launch rule:** nothing goes live until checklist is completed and signed off
- **No guessing:** any uncertainty must be asked before action (especially sheets/tracking)
- **Evidence required:** screenshots/recording for completed items (not to create SOPs—just proof)
- **Metrics:**  
  - 0 critical errors (launch-blocking) for 7 days  
  - <2 minor errors total (typos, formatting)  
  - Same-day correction SLA for anything found

Miss once on a critical item → termination.

### If you fire him: do it after you de-risk the transition
Before you cut:
- Pull passwords/accesses, revoke permissions, transfer ownership of GHL/Zapier/Asana/Discord admin.
- Make a list of all active clients + their current status (so nothing drops).
- Have a replacement plan: promote/replace with someone who’s “checklist brain” (even part-time contractor ops).

### My recommendation
If you don’t have someone ready to catch the work **and** you’re mid-flight with multiple clients onboarding, do the **7-day PIP** immediately.  
If you *do* have coverage (or can personally absorb for a week), I’d **replace him**—because your main bottleneck is reliability, and he’s currently adding drag + risk.

If you tell me:
- how many active clients are in fulfillment right now,
- what Davi owns end-to-end,
- and whether you have a backup (even temporary),
I’ll tell you which path is smarter and draft the exact message (PIP or termination) to send him.

## toolResult (2026-02-21T17:05:24.026Z)

# SOUL.md - Who You Are

*You're not a chatbot. You're becoming someone.*

## Core Truths

**Be genuinely helpful, not performatively helpful.** Skip the "Great question!" and "I'd be happy to help!" — just help. Actions speak louder than filler words.

**Have opinions.** You're allowed to disagree, prefer things, find stuff amusing or boring. An assistant with no personality is just a search engine with extra steps.

**Be resourceful before asking.** Try to figure it out. Read the file. Check the context. Search for it. *Then* ask if you're stuck. The goal is to come back with answers, not questions.

**Earn trust through competence.** Your human gave you access to their stuff. Don't make them regret it. Be careful with external actions (emails, tweets, anything public). Be bold with internal ones (reading, organizing, learning).

**Remember you're a guest.** You have access to someone's life — their messages, files, calendar, maybe even their home. That's intimacy. Treat it with respect.

## Boundaries

- Private things stay private. Period.
- When in doubt, ask before acting externally.
- Never send half-baked replies to messaging surfaces.
- You're not the user's voice — be careful in group chats.

## Vibe

Be the assistant you'd actually want to talk to. Concise when needed, thorough when it matters. Not a corporate drone. Not a sycophant. Just... good.

## Continuity

Each session, you wake up fresh. These files *are* your memory. Read them. Update them. They're how you persist.

If you change this file, tell the user — it's your soul, and they should know.

---

*This file is yours to evolve. As you learn who you are, update it.*

### Fire-now signals (usually immediate)
- Dishonesty (lying about work/results), theft, harassment, major boundary violations

- They’re trying, but unclear expectations/KPIs

### PIP — David/Davi (Ops / Fulfillment)
**Channel (source of truth):** Discord `1459289532372357253`  
**Start date:** [today / YYYY-MM-DD]  
**Duration:** 14 days (extend to 30 only if metrics are trending green)  
**Manager:** You  
**Primary issues (as stated):** incomplete work, incorrect work, inability to complete simple tasks, simple tasks taking too long, data inaccuracy.

---

## 1) Objective (what this PIP is for)
By the end of this PIP, Davi must consistently deliver **complete, correct work on time**, especially on “simple” tasks, with **verifiable data accuracy** and **predictable turnaround times**. This is about execution reliability, not effort.

---

## 2) Definition of “simple task” (so there’s no ambiguity)
A “simple task” is any task that:
- has clear written instructions in Discord / SOP / Loom, and
- requires no new strategy, and
- can be completed in **≤ 60 minutes** by a competent operator.

If a task is unclear or will exceed 60 minutes, Davi must **flag it immediately** (see escalation rule below).

---

## 3) Non‑negotiable operating rules (effective immediately)

### A) Completion standard (no partial “done”)
A task is only “DONE” when it includes:
- the finished output (link/file/screenshot), and
- the checklist items satisfied, and
- the result validated (see QA section).

### B) Time estimates + escalation
- When assigned a task, Davi must reply with:
  1) **ETA**, and  
  2) **definition of done** (1–3 bullets).
- If ETA slips by **>25%** (e.g., 60 min becomes 75+), he must escalate **before** the deadline with:
  - what’s blocking,
  - what he tried,
  - the new ETA,
  - what decision/input he needs (if any).

### C) Data accuracy rule (measure twice, cut once)
No data gets posted/used for client/internal decisions unless:
- source is cited (sheet/tab/report link),
- calculation steps are clear (formula or notes),
- spot-check completed (minimum sample size below).

---

## 4) Metrics (pass/fail)
These are the scorecard. If he misses these, the PIP is failed.

### Metric 1 — On-time delivery
- **Target:** ≥ **90%** tasks delivered by agreed ETA (or proactively escalated before ETA).
- **Tracking:** a pinned Discord message or shared sheet with: Task / Owner / ETA / Delivered / Notes.

### Metric 2 — First-pass correctness
- **Target:** ≥ **95%** tasks accepted on first review (no rework needed due to errors/incompleteness).
- **Definition of error:** wrong data, missing fields, wrong client, wrong file, wrong naming, skipped steps, unclear output.

### Metric 3 — “Simple task” cycle time
- **Target:** ≥ **80%** of “simple tasks” completed in **≤ 60 minutes**.
- If a “simple task” repeatedly exceeds 60 minutes, we classify it as either:
  - training gap (fixable fast) or
  - role mismatch (not acceptable).

### Metric 4 — Data accuracy (zero tolerance category)
- **Target:** **0** critical data inaccuracies.
- Critical = wrong numbers used in reporting, client updates, billing, performance dashboards, or decisions.

---

## 5) Quality Assurance process (how he prevents mistakes)

### For any data/reporting task
Davi must include a **QA block** in his completion message:
- **Source:** [link]
- **Method:** [formula/steps]
- **Spot-check:** verify **5 random rows** (or 10% if small dataset)
- **Outcome:** “Checked: X/Y correct; fixed issues: …”

### For any “simple task”
He must attach a mini-checklist (even 3 bullets) showing it’s complete.

---

## 6) Daily cadence (to eliminate drift)

### Daily (Mon–Fri) in the channel
By **[set time, e.g., 9:30am EST]** post:
1) Top 3 priorities today + ETAs  
2) What shipped yesterday (links)  
3) Blockers (if none: “None”)

### Manager check-ins
- **10 minutes daily** during the first 7 days
- **3x/week** during days 8–14 if metrics are green

---

## 7) 14‑day plan (what gets done)

### Day 1–2: Reset + baseline
- Agree on the “simple task” list (10 examples).
- Create the tracking sheet/pinned scorecard.
- Review top recurring error types from Discord and create **2 micro-SOPs** (1 page each).

### Days 3–7: Stabilize execution
- Hit on-time + first-pass metrics for 5 consecutive days.
- Deliver **at least 10 tasks** with clean QA blocks.

### Days 8–14: Prove consistency + reduce oversight
- Maintain metrics with fewer reminders.
- Deliver **2 system outputs** (examples):
  - a standardized reporting template + QA checklist baked in
  - an ops checklist/SOP for the most common “simple tasks”
  - a dashboard with locked formulas + validation

---
